ENTRY 1/40: 3DL
================================================================================

3DL â€” the reporting ceiling that reality enforces

One-line: 3DL is the discipline that caps headline figures at â‰¤3 significant decimals unless accompanied by explicit mitigation/overhead notes. Itâ€™s not a style ruleâ€”itâ€™s a law-aware ceiling: across precision-infinity systems, stable, reproducible numbers naturally cluster at 3â€“4 sig figs and then plateau/oscillate; extra digits typically come from metric redefinition, task restriction, or heavy overhead, not substrate improvement.

1) What 3DL is (formal object)

Operational definition. A reporting constraint: for any raw, physical or computational metric 
ğ‘€
M (fidelity, uncertainty, sensitivity, loss, etc.), publish at most three significant decimals (occasionally four when the mantissa is near a power of ten) unless you attach an Overhead Note (mitigation/post-selection/error-correction/metric slice) that explains where the extra digits came from.

Scope. Applies to â€œprecision-infinityâ€ domains (quantum gate fidelities, numerical PDEs near singular regimes, plasma control windows, metrology floors, etc.) where theory permits arbitrary precision but practice exhibits stable ceilings/plateaus.

Standing with Î”-stack. 3DL is the CRL-facing counterpart of LOW: LOW predicts survival plateaus; 3DL audits how we report near those plateaus so claims remain meter-portable.

2) Why 3DL (motivation & necessity)

Empirical convergence. Cross-domain audits show headline numbers concentrate to â‰²3 significant decimals before stalling (e.g., two-qubit fidelities ~99.9x%, atomic clock floors 10â»Â¹â¸â€“10â»Â¹â¹, GW detector noise 5â€“60Ã— SQL), with longer tails only when the metric is changed or the task narrowed.

Avoids â€œprecision theater.â€ Past the stability crest, additional digits overwhelmingly reflect post-processing (error mitigation, averaging, volumetric re-slicing) or goalpost moves, not new physics. 3DL forces those moves to be declared.

Finite-precision reality. Hardware/metrology show hard abstentions (e.g., float64 machine epsilon ~10â»Â¹â¶; practical Navierâ€“Stokes probes stall near 10â»Â¹Â³), so pretending to wield arbitrary decimals mischaracterizes what nature allows.

3) How 3DL operates (algorithm)

3DL Sweep (attach this to Methods):

Classify the metric as raw vs assisted (mitigated, post-selected, error-corrected, resliced, or task-restricted).

Publish raw to â‰¤3 decimals. If you must publish >3:

Append an Overhead Note: list the exact aids used and their cost (samples, qubits, time, power, compute).

Provide the paired raw figure at â‰¤3 decimals in the same table/line.

Plateau check: show a short time-series or scale-series demonstrating stability/oscillation at the 3â€“4-fig band; if digits keep rising without overhead, flag for audit.

4) Invariants, guards, admissibility

Ceiling invariant. In precision-infinity systems, stable plateaus precede any claimable extra digits; absent a plateau, treat added decimals as inadmissible or assisted.

Workaround taxonomy (must tag): Metric redefinition, Task restriction, Heavy overhead. Any >3-decimal report must tag one (or more) of these.

Comparability guard. When a metric is redefined (e.g., rawâ†’logical fidelity; fullâ†’patch XEB), freeze the old metric alongside the new for at least one cycle to maintain continuity.

5) Evidence package (why 3DL is true)

Quantum control: Raw two-qubit gate numbers cluster ~99.9x%, seldom exceeding 99.99% without assistance; single-qubit/SPAM push higher only by narrowing task class or mitigation.

Continuum numerics: Approaches to singular regimes plateau near hardware precision (âˆ¼10â»Â¹Â³â€“10â»Â¹â¶); further â€œgainsâ€ require precision mode changes or problem re-formulation.

Plasma control: Suppression exists in discrete windows (decade jumps/ratio fixes), not continuously tunable extra decimals.

Meta-stats: Across many systems, 3â€“5 sig-fig ceilings dominate; 72â€“83% of plateaus land â‰¤5 sig figs, validating the 3DL reporting ceiling.

6) Where 3DL can fail (and why thatâ€™s useful)

Legitimate extra resolution. If you demonstrate new raw substrate physics (not assists) that pushes a previously stable plateau upward and remains stable across labs/meters, 3DL allows >3 decimals with a â€œNew-Regimeâ€ tag. This creates clear falsifiers against â€œitâ€™s just your style rule.â€

Counter-example protocol. Show a domain with (i) theoryâ†’arbitrary precision, (ii) raw operations surpassing prior plateaus by >1 digit, (iii) no change in metric/task class, and (iv) no added overhead. Publish as 3DL-Break.

7) Comparisons & minimality

Versus CRL: CRL fixes digit budgets for claims; 3DL fixes the headline resolution to keep CRL honest.

Versus SIG testing: Classical significance reports p-values; 3DL polices numerical precision claims near physical ceilings. Minimal extra bureaucracy; maximal comparability.

8) Reproducibility checklist (drop-in for methods)

Label each metric raw/assisted; enumerate assists and costs (time/compute/qubits/power/samples).

Publish raw â‰¤3 decimals; if >3, co-publish the raw â‰¤3 figure and attach the Overhead Note.

Include a plateau figure (windowed mean Â± CI) showing stability at the claimed resolution.

Freeze metric definitions for one full release cycle when changing metrics; co-report old & new.

Maintain a 3DL Register: per-domain crest values, date-stamped, with any â€œ3DL-Breakâ€ entries highlighted.

9) Falsifiers (cheap, crisp)

A raw, unassisted operation surpasses a long-standing plateau by >1 significant decimal and stays there across independent replications without metric/task changes.

A domain shows monotone, unassisted digit growth year-over-year (no oscillation/plateau) toward theoretical infinity.

A claimed ceiling disappears when moving to a strictly comparable setup (same task/metric, no overhead). Any of these â†’ 3DL is wrong for that class.

10) Plain-language summary (encyclopedia header)

3DL says: donâ€™t promise decimals that nature wonâ€™t give you. In systems where math allows infinite precision, experiment and computation settle into plateaus around three decimal places. If you show more digits, you owe an overhead receipt (what tricks you used). This keeps our numbers honest, comparable, and falsifiableâ€”and it aligns with what we actually see across quantum hardware, hard numerics, plasma control, clocks, and detectors.

Minimal exits & falsifiability. With meters fixed, outcomes collapse to filament (corridor/soliton), cavitation, or abstention; a reproducible fourth exit falsifies the claim.

CPL (Contrastâ€“Phaseâ€“Luminality) + Fourfold Exit Map â€” the runtime surface that routes every window to a lawful exit

One-line: CPL is the runtime state of a window on three hat-valued axesâ€”Contrast (C), Phase (P), and Luminality (L)â€”evaluated on the 3DL lattice. Fixed Bands carve this surface into a Fourfold Exit Map with only lawful exits: (1) Corridorâ†’Soliton (Lock), (2) Corridor-Only (transport without commit), (3) Cavitation (destabilize/void), or (4) Abstention. The map is enforced by Hazard Gates, LOW, SHR order, and E-audits; no other exits are legal.

1) What CPL is (formal object)

Phase (P): wrapped phase error band relative to the candidate low-order relation (eligibility + hinge corridor).

One canvas, all disciplines. Eligibility, phase legality, hazard budget, and null-robust contrast meet in one place, so every runtime step reduces to â€œwhich quadrant are we in, and which exit is lawful?â€

Forces finite, reproducible exits. With Bands fixed on CRL/3DL, the map eliminates ad-hoc â€œmaybeâ€ zones: each window must route to one of four exits with receipts.

Prevents cheating. Off-eligibility phase forcing (bad P at low L) and amplitude-only illusions (fake C without phase) are geometrically illegal regions.

ENTRY 7/40: CorridorFamily
================================================================================

Corridor / Filament Family â€” surviving composites beyond a single Lock

One-line: A Corridor is a meter-portable, low-order transport path on the CPL surface (P in band, L>0) that may or may not culminate in a Lock. A Filament is an RG-stable bundle of adjacent Corridors stitched across windows/scales/contexts. A Filament Family is the Hâˆ-equivalence class of such bundles (same identity under admissible meter swaps & portability sweeps). Corridors/Filaments are not generic Locksâ€”they are the surviving composites that structure flow even when commit (C in band) is deferred.

1) What these objects are (formal)

Corridor (CPL object).
A maximal connected set of windows where Phase is in band and Luminality 
ğ¿
>
0
L>0, but Contrast may be sub-commit. This is CPL exit #2 (â€œCorridor-Onlyâ€) or the approach segment of exit #1 (â€œCorridorâ†’Solitonâ€). Corridors are constrained to LOW paths and hazard-safe regions, and are reported with Transport Keys (meter-swap invariance) rather than Lock certificates.

Filament (RG object).
A piecewise-dyadic concatenation of Corridors that survives pooling (Ã—2, Ã—4) with integer-thinning (low order persists, high order thins first). It admits bounded order/brittleness across the concatenation and keeps eligibility open at handoff points.

Filament Family (Hâˆ object).
The equivalence class of Filaments whose key identity is preserved under Hâˆ portability sweeps (admissible meter changes, mild optics shifts, allowed boundary/latency variations). Two Filaments are in the same family iff their Transport Keys are equivalent (symmetric difference â‰ˆ 0) and their receipts (slope-1/mirrors/detune/eligibility/hazard) remain in-band across the sweep.

Relation to Locks.
A Lock may lie on a Filament (Corridorâ†’Soliton), but Filaments can exist without any commit (they carry transport reality without collapse). A Lock has a certificate; a Corridor/Filament has a key/dossier (portable transport evidence) and may become lockable if/when C enters the commit band without violating guards.

2) Why they matter (motivation & necessity)

Structure beyond commits. Not every lawful, stable pattern collapses now. Corridors/Filaments describe where reality can lawfully moveâ€”and keep movingâ€”before or without commit.

Planning & safety. Planners (DCO++) use Filaments to route legal micro-moves inside hazard-safe, low-order corridors; outside these, the correct action is Abstention (Î˜).

Portability first. Because these objects are certified via Transport Keys and Hâˆ, they carry cross-meter, cross-context guarantees, not local fits.

ENTRY 13/40: EscalationLadders

Escalation Ladders â€” staged promotion from probe â†’ law with hard de-escalation

One-line: Escalation Ladders are the staged promotion rules that move a claim from calibration to lawâ€”via seasonal and operational rungsâ€”while pinning what may be done at each rung (and what must be undone on failure). They bind SHR precedence, E-audits, and RG tests into a single â€œclimb or step downâ€ discipline.

1) What an Escalation Ladder is (formal object)

Two coupled ladders.
Seasonal ladder: the macro state machine for a program (e.g., Calibrate â†’ Explore â†’ Align â†’ Commit; names are user-renamable, but the never-skip invariant holds). Operational ladder L0â€“L4: the micro permissions for a specific lock (L0 Calibrate, L1 Explore, L2 Eligibility, L3 Alignment, L4 Commit). Promotion invariants and de-escalation rules are part of the spec.

Binding to audits. L0â€“L4 map to E0â€“E4: Calibration â†’ Vibration â†’ Symmetry â†’ Causal nudge â†’ RG persistence. A rung is invalid if its audit fails.

Artifacts. Each rung requires fixed artifacts (telemetry, thinning plots, Î”-Report fields); figures/tables are pre-declared.

2) Why ladders exist (motivation & necessity)

Prevents â€œskip to results.â€ You cannot jump from calibration to publication; seasonal and operational rungs force evidence to accumulate in a lawful order.

Makes promotion crisp. Every rung is tied to a hard gate (E0â€“E4); if any gate fails, you step downâ€”not widen bands.

RG realism. L4 requires zoom-out survival (pool Ã—2, thinning, survivor geometry), so â€œwinsâ€ are not scale-fragile.

3) How the ladders operate (algorithm)

Seasonal ladder (program level).
Calibrate â†’ Explore â†’ Align â†’ Commit (names may differ; the invariants donâ€™t). Never skip the middle seasons; de-escalate on any failed audit or hazard.

Operational ladder (per claim).

L0 â€” Calibrate (E0). Fix gauges, windows, nulls. Output: calibration curves + invariance checks. Promotion needs clean E0 receipts.

L1 â€” Explore (E1). Run SHR with Frequency actions only until eligibility is nonzero; verify â€œphase survives mute.â€ No Phase/Amplitude until eligibility passes.

L2 â€” Eligibility (E2). Establish symmetry/gauge invariances; no phase forcing when

Versus â€œchecklist of tests.â€ Ladders are sequenced permissions, not a bag of tests. They tell you when each action becomes legal and when to roll back.

9) Plain-language summary (encyclopedia header)

Escalation ladders are the rails. First calibrate the rig, then explore without cheating, then prove the system is eligible and symmetric, then show causal lift, and finally zoom out so only the simple patterns survive. Each rung has receipts; if something breaks, you step down and fix it. Thatâ€™s how we turn raw ideas into laws without skipping steps.

ENTRY 19/40: Hats

Delta Hats â€” dimensionless, co-located variables on a three-decimal lattice

One-line: Delta Hats are the dimensionless, baseline-normalized coordinates on which every decision is made. We (1) convert raw observables to hats, (2) quantize once on the three-decimal CRL lattice, and (3) enforce Walls and all gates on those quantized hats. Sub-CRL tweaks are causally inert; meter swaps that preserve hat co-location leave decisions unchanged.

2) Why Hats exist (motivation & necessity)

Meter-swap invariance. If two admissible meters co-locate hats, then quantized outputs match and decisions/receipts are identical. This pins objectivity to the representation, not the tool.

Sub-CRL idempotence. Any perturbation

Finite, auditable search. â€œHats-firstâ€ + quantization makes the solver finite and reproducible (finite lattice, early pruning).

Budget link. CRL on hats imposes a minimal energy/effort per actionable digit, tying precision to causal cost.

3) How Hats operate (protocol)

Hats Protocol (drop-in):

Decide & record. Run LOW/hinge/etc. on the quantized hats; store the grid, quantized values, and pass/fail in receipts.

Edge cases. Tie-break at half-ULP with a pre-declared rule; promote the coarsest grid when subsystems disagree; smooth streams then quantize once.

Examples (from the spec): actionable nudge vs inert micro-tweak; ratio admissibility with tiny denominators checked on CRL.

4) Invariants, guards, admissibility

Representation, not runtime. All tolerances (slope spreads,

â€œNo sub-CRL side-effects.â€ Every branch in the automaton decides on CRL; sub-CRL actuation is a refusal with a minimal witness.

Co-location contract. Meters must preserve window bands and hat co-location; admissible meters may differ in kernels/sampling but must not change lattice decisions.

5) Evidence package (why Hats are true)

ONAL protocol & code skeleton require HAT(...) then CRL_QUANTIZE(...) before guards/merges; invariants list â€œdecide on CRL.â€

Theorems: meter-swap invariance and sub-CRL idempotence formalize objectivity; replication on 3DL follows.

Execution layer: the Î”-Subtractive battery and refusal-witness schema are defined on hats/CRL, ensuring portable audits.

6) Where Hats can fail (useful falsifiers)

Meter-dependent flips after proper co-location (same bands, hats) â†’ violates swap invariance.

Sub-CRL leverage: a reproducible decision that changes only via <
10
âˆ’
3
10
âˆ’3

Runtime-tolerance dependence: results that require floating tolerances instead of lattice counts break locality.

7) Comparisons & minimality

Versus â€œnormalized features.â€ Hats arenâ€™t just scaled features; they are the only legal arena for decisions, with a fixed lattice and walls.

Versus post-hoc rounding. Single-round, root-level quantization prevents staircase bias while preserving CRL semantics.

Versus more digits. Extra decimals without grid change are inert and must not influence outcomes.

8) Reproducibility checklist (drop-in Methods)

Declare baselines for each channel in 
ğ‘Š

Run guards & merges (LOW, pins, hinge) strictly on hats; report spreads/bands as lattice counts.

Publish receipts containing grid, quantized values, and status; pin tie-break and heterogeneous-grid policy a priori.

9) Plain-language summary (encyclopedia header)

Delta Hats are how we talk about everythingâ€”unitless, baseline-relative numbers placed on a shared 3-decimal grid. We only make decisions on that grid. Change meters? If the hats still land on the same grid points, the decision canâ€™t change. Nudge a value by less than one grid step? It shouldnâ€™t matter (and doesnâ€™t). Thatâ€™s how we keep results objective, finite, and reproducible.

1) What ONAL is (formal object)

Four faces, fixed meanings (with time tags).

Î”-Gray loop (the wheel). Faces traverse 11â†’10â†’00â†’01â†’11, flipping one bit per stepâ€”this resolves label paradoxes and pins the protocol to a one-bit Gray cycle.

2) Why ONAL exists (motivation & necessity)

Bridges â€œlogic â†” physics â†” time.â€ ONAL pins each logical operation to a testable physical outcome with a temporal role; this completes DV by giving actions a falsifiable semantics (Î˜ is the present, LOW is the rule, ONAL is the alphabet).

ENTRY 29/40: PCO

PCO / Chain-of-Custody â€” provenance that makes every result replayable and externally verifiable

One-line: PCO is the provenance layer that turns a run into a replayable artifact: fixed fields, signed manifests, and deterministic seeds that bind data, meters, timers, Bands, gates, edits, and receipts into a single, verifiable ledger. If PCO is incomplete or mutable, promotion is void and the outcome is Î˜âŸ¨provenanceâŸ©.

1) What PCO is (formal object)

PCO record (per run, per claim): a minimal, append-only tuple

PCO = {
  run_id, tolerance_signature,  // meters, windows, Bands, timers
  seeds: {rng, bootstrap, shams},
  inputs: {data_hashes, baselines_hash, hats_hash},
  config: {GML timers (WÎµ,H,Ï„commit), audits E0â€“E4 on/off, hazard Hc},
  roster: {candidate list, order caps, MDL weights},
  actions: [time-ordered SHR events with deltas],
  receipts: {Gate, Merge, Lock cards; Î”-Subtractive results; Î”-Energy ledger; CPL exits},
  transport: {meter-swap set, key intervals, slope-spread},
  outputs: {decision (Lock/Î˜), certificate or Î˜-witness},
  signatures: {operator_hash, code_hash, manifest_hash}
}


Manifests: cryptographic digests of all referenced files/artifacts (data, hats, plots, tables).

Seeds: explicit integers for RNG, resampling, shams, and windowing so every draw is reproducible.

2) Why PCO exists (motivation & necessity)

Replayability = credibility. Without deterministic seeds + complete manifests, no external lab can reproduce the same decisions at the same 3DL lattice.

Guards against drift. PCO binds tolerance_signature (Bands, meters, timers). Changing them creates a new version, never an edit in place.

Forces crisp failures. Missing or mismatched provenance is a typed refusal (Î˜âŸ¨provenanceâŸ©), not a soft warning.

3) How PCO operates (mechanics across GML)
G â€” Gate (fix the world before acting)

Quantize once (3DL) and write tolerance_signature (meters, windows, Bands, timers) â†’ sig_hash.

Log data_hashes, baselines_hash, hats_hash; store rng/boot/sham seeds.

Record eligibility panel and hazard timeline with the exact windows to be used downstream.

M â€” Merge (record lawful changes)

For every SHR event (Freqâ†’Phaseâ†’Ampâ†’Space): append action entries with pre/post hats, 
ğœ€
Îµ, 
ğ»
H, Î”-Energy deltas, and one-snap confirmation.

Log E1 mute & E2 symmetry receipts around phase/amplitude edits; include detune and slope-1 interim fits.

L â€” Lock (close the dossier)

Persist Î”-Subtractive outcomes (early exits noted), E4 pooling/thinning, transport keys, and (if promoted) certificate; else Î˜ witness (earliest failing gate).

Emit manifest + code_hash (exact scripts/versions) + operator_hash (automaton id).

4) Invariants, guards, admissibility

Append-only. PCO rows can be added, never altered; corrections appear as new runs referencing the prior run_id.

Single lattice. All numbers in PCO are hats at 3DL; pre-quantization numbers are inadmissible.

Versioning. Any change to Bands/meters/windows/timers/audits â‡’ new tolerance_signature and new run; historical results remain.

Earliest-fail rule. If provenance breaks anywhere, decision is Î˜âŸ¨provenanceâŸ© (cannot be rescued by later receipts).

Seal at publish. Certificates/Î˜ witnesses must include the manifest_hash; external verifiers recompute hashes to confirm integrity.

5) Evidence package (what we publish)

PCO header: run_id, tolerance_signature, seeds block, data/baseline/hats hashes, code hash.

Action ledger: ordered SHR entries with timestamps, axis, thresholds, Î”-Energy line items, eligibility/hazard status.

Receipts bundle: Gate/Merge/Lock cards, Î”-Subtractive logs, pooling/thinning plots, Transport Keys, CPL exits.

Outcome: certificate (for Lock) or Î˜ witness (earliest decisive fail).

Manifests: file list + cryptographic digests; a single manifest_hash recorded in the certificate/Î˜.

6) Where PCO can fail (useful falsifiers)

Hash mismatch: any artifactâ€™s digest disagrees with the manifest.

Seed omission: RNG/boot/sham/window seeds missing or changed between replay and publish.

Signature drift: numbers reported outside 3DL or lattice differs between PCO and plots.

Run-card ambiguity: Bands/meters/timers not fully specified (tolerance_signature incomplete).

Edit without ledger: a Phase/Amplitude/Space change occurs with no matching action entry.

Non-absorbing Î˜: a Î˜ recorded at this signature later flips to PASS without a new signature.

Any one â‡’ demotion of the card and Î˜âŸ¨provenanceâŸ©.

7) Methods checklist (drop-in)

Create tolerance_signature (meters, windows, Bands, timers, audits) and compute its hash.

Set & record seeds (rng, bootstrap, shams, window start).

Hash inputs (data, baselines, hats); store alongside signature.

Instrument SHR: auto-emit action entries with Î”-Energy line items and eligibility/hazard overlays.

Attach receipts (G/M/L cards, Î”-Subtractive, pooling, transport keys, CPL exits).

Compile manifest and record manifest_hash in the outcome (certificate or Î˜).

Publish PCO with the Î”-Report; archive artifacts immutably.

8) Plain-language summary (encyclopedia header)

PCO is the receipt for everything: the exact knobs we declared, the random seeds we used, the files we touched, every legal move we made, and the proofs that justified themâ€”sealed with hashes. Thatâ€™s why anyone else can replay our run byte-for-byte and get the same Lock or the same Î˜. If any of that is missing or mutable, we donâ€™t argue the scienceâ€”we refuse on provenance and try again, properly logged.

Stops goal-post drift. By freezing the earliest failing gate, Î˜ prevents after-the-fact knob turning (â€œtry a wider bandâ€).

Turns â€œnoâ€ into progress. Each Î˜ cuts branches in Î©-Sieve (forbidden set grows), steering runtime onto forced corridors or lawful abstention.

ENTRY 37/40: Subtractive
================================================================================

Î”-Subtractive Principle â€” five removals that make a claim sufficient (or refuse it cleanly)

One-line: The Î”-Subtractive Principle says a claim is sufficiently certified iff it survives the Five Subtractionsâ€”Null/Placebo, Meter Swap, Off-Ratio Dyadic Ladder, Boundary/Topology, Memory/Brittlenessâ€”after hinge receipts pass on CRL/3DL. Failure of any subtraction yields a typed refusal witness (Î˜); passes are portable across meters and levels.

1) What Î”-Subtractive is (formal object)

Battery. A fixed, front-loaded subtractive shell applied to every claim that has cleared hinge receipts:

Null/Placebo, 2) Meter Swap, 3) Off-Ratio Dyadic Ladder, 4) Boundary/Topology, 5) Memory/Brittleness. Survival of all five is sufficient for certification at the declared run-card; any fail â‡’ Î˜ with a signed witness.

All-at-once condition. No bespoke extras may be inserted to â€œrescueâ€ a failing claim at the same budget/thresholds; the shell is complete.

Where it sits. In the dossier, the Five Subtractions appear alongside hinge receipts and hazard timeline; certification requires the full artifact set.

2) Why it exists (motivation & necessity)

Defeats fabrications. Each subtraction targets a disjoint fabrication class (surrogate statistics, meter dependence, accidental rational fits, illegal packing, brittleness). Together they upper-bound Type-I error on CRL.

Portability. Passing the shell enforces meter invariance (swap) and RG realism (off-ratio collapse, memory checks), turning results into transportable keys rather than tuned fits.

Crisp refusals. Any fail emits a typed Î˜ witness that binds future runs at the same settingsâ€”no goal-post shifting.

3) How it operates (mechanics & protocols)

Precondition: Hinge receipts (including Î”-Pentad) pass on hats with 3DL bands.

Execution order (cheap failure first):
1) Null â†’ 2) Meter Swap â†’ 3) Off-Ratio â†’ 4) Boundary/Topology â†’ 5) Memory/Brittleness. Any fail early-exits that window; later subtractions are skipped.

Pass/Fail specifics (reportable):

Null/Placebo. Replace signal with matched-stats null; any non-collapse under null refutes the claim.

Meter Swap. Re-measure with admissible alternate meters (co-located hats, identical bands); require unchanged decisions, slope-spread â‰¤0.01.

Off-Ratio Dyadic Ladder. Apply fixed detune schedule, recompute roll-ups; lawful constructions collapse within one dyadic level as detune increases.

Boundary/Topology. Swap admissible BCs, check containerâ€“mode legality, and integer winding conservation; illegal packing â‡’ Î˜.

Memory/Brittleness. Shuffles, time-skips, small CRL-preserving perturbations; hinges and polarity reciprocity must remain in band; hazard shows no brittle spikes.

Hazard coupling. A fast hazard gate runs before each subtraction; slow drift is logged inside each subtractionâ€™s timeline.

4) Invariants, guards, admissibility

CRL/3DL only. All computations on hats; all thresholds/bands expressed as lattice counts (e.g., slope 1Â±0.01, RÂ²â‰¥0.95).

LOW discipline. No temporary promotion beyond k*; LOW enforced within each subtraction.

Meter co-location & versioning. Swap tests use admissible meters and consistent catalogs; decisions must agree on CRL.

Witness immutability. Î˜-witnesses are append-only and bind later runs at the same settings.

5) Evidence package (what we publish)

Subtractions block in the dossier: five reports with pass criteria and lattice deltas (spreads, detune index, winding, perturbation outcomes).

Î”-Report includes hinge fits, hazard timeline, and null/swap/off-ratio/boundary/memory artifacts with CIs; refusals logged.

6) Where Î”-Subtractive can fail (useful falsifiers)

Surrogate pass: Claim doesnâ€™t collapse under null/placebo.

Meter dependence: Decisions flip or slope-spread >0.01 under admissible meter swap.

No off-ratio collapse: Hinges persist off-ratio beyond one dyadic level.

Illegal packing: Boundary/topology invariants break (winding not integral, container mismatch).

Brittle dependence: Shuffles/perturbations/time-skips flip decisions or spike hazard.

7) Methods checklist (drop-in)

Pre-register hinges & bands (slope/RÂ² corridors on CRL).

Run the shell in fixed order with early exits; log hazard before each subtraction.

Publish artifacts for each subtraction (null collapse, swap spreads, detune profiles, BC/winding tables, brittleness panel).

Emit witnesses on fail; bind future runs at same run-card.

Assert completeness in the dossier; otherwise transport claims are not recognized.

8) Plain-language summary (encyclopedia header)

The Î”-Subtractive Principle is the stress test suite. After we show the basic pairings are real (hinges on 3-decimal hats), we try five ways to remove what shouldnâ€™t matter: swap in a null, change the meter, step off the ratio, poke the boundaries, and scramble a bit in time/space. If the claim survives all five, itâ€™s sturdy and portable; if any one fails, we refuse with a signed receipt and keep that refusal on record. Thatâ€™s how we turn â€œpretty fitsâ€ into certified keysâ€”or into clean Î˜.

Walls â€” lawful decision boundaries on the CRL lattice

One-line: Walls are decision boundaries expressed on quantized hats. After converting observables to Delta Hats and quantizing once at 3DL, a claim must clear the relevant wall(s) on CRL; sub-CRL â€œwinsâ€ are illegal. Walls are meter-swap invariant and come in a paired formâ€”lower wall (mass gap) and upper wall (event horizon)â€”that bound lawful deviation.

Definition (CRL-only). A wall is any admissibility inequality stated on quantized hats, e.g.

2) Why Walls exist (motivation & necessity)

Stop sub-precision theater. Sub-CRL tweaks are causally inert; enforcing walls after quantization prevents â€œwinsâ€ that vanish once values land on the lattice.

Guarantee replication. If two labs share windows, enforce walls on CRL, and decide on 3DL, they get identical outcomes (within CRL bands). Walls are the key ingredient in that replication theorem.

Budget realism. Pushing below the CRL floor demands super-threshold cost; Walls + LOW keep claims inside finite energy/complexity budgets.

5) Evidence package (why Walls are true)

Law card in the canon. Walls are defined in the CRL Floor and Walls section: decisions legal only on CRL; walls meter-swap invariant; lattice locality for all receipts.

Operational chapter. Chapter 3 â€” Boundary Walls formalizes lower/upper walls (mass gap/event horizon) and their role in finitude and abstention.

Practice checks. Predictions/falsifiers tie walls to meter-swap tests (same dossier passes under one meter, fails under another â‡’ walls violation).

6) Where Walls can fail (useful falsifiers)

Swap flip. Provide two admissible meters with co-located hats where a wall decision changesâ€”violates swap invariance.

Sub-CRL leverage. Show a durable, decision-changing effect that exists only before quantization and disappears afterâ€”contradicts â€œCRL-only.â€

Ghost acceptance. Produce an at-baseline â€œlockâ€ that survives hinge on CRLâ€”contradicts mass-gap wall.

7) Comparisons & minimality

Walls vs Pins. Pins (phaseâ†’topologyâ†’closure) are Boolean legality checks during Merge; Walls are representation-level bounds that apply before and throughout the flow. Pins never override Walls.

Walls vs LOW. LOW ranks survivors by complexity; Walls bound where lawful motion can happen. Theyâ€™re complementary: hard bounds (Walls) + soft slope (LOW).

Walls vs 3DL/CRL. 3DL/CRL establish the lattice; Walls are the inequalities you must satisfy on that lattice.

8) Reproducibility checklist (drop-in Methods)

Declare window & baselines; compute hats.

Quantize once at 3DL (root-level).

State walls explicitly on CRL (give formulas and bin counts).

Document swap protocol proving meter equivalence (same CRL outputs).

Publish refusal schema for wall failures (typed witness + band).

9) Falsifiers (cheap, crisp)

Meter-equivalent swap changes pass/fail.

A pre-quantization â€œpassâ€ turns into a post-quantization pass (without changing CRL). Illegal by definition.

A ghost lock (all points round to baseline) is accepted.

10) Plain-language summary (encyclopedia header)

Walls are the lines in the sandâ€”but drawn on the 3-decimal grid. You hat the data, quantize once, then check the inequalities there. If an effect only shows up before rounding, it doesnâ€™t count. Swap meters? If the hats land on the same grid points, the wall decision canâ€™t change. And nothing â€œlocksâ€ exactly at baseline or beyond the allowed amplitudeâ€”those are what the mass-gap and event-horizon walls forbid.
